You said:
Implementing procedural generation (PCG) for a space-themed world requires a modular, rule-based approach to ensure consistency, scalability, and performance. Best practices include using noise functions (Perlin/Simplex) for terrain, assembling ships/stations from predefined component libraries based on functional logic, and defining constraint-based rules for weapon placement and scaling. 
University of Waterloo
University of Waterloo
 +2
1. Space Ships & Stations (Scalability & Modular Assembly)
Modular Assembly (Constructive): Build ships using a "lego-set" approach. Create libraries of parts (bridges, hull segments, engine modules) that connect via predefined attachment points (sockets).
Functional Logic: Instead of purely random generation, use logic: small ships get few, high-maneuverability parts; large capital ships require engine blocks proportional to their mass.
Hierarchical Structure: Define a ship's frame (main hull) first, then attach sub-modules (weapons, shields), and finally greeble (small aesthetic details) for visual density.
Scaling: Use a base design and apply scalar multipliers for size, then automatically scale the count of turrets and engines to match. 
Reddit
Reddit
 +4
2. Weapon System Generation
Constraint-Based Mounting: Create sockets on ship modules labeled "Weapon_Small," "Weapon_Large." The generator only places appropriate weapon assets on these nodes.
Ratios: Balance firepower by defining a ratio (e.g., weapon capacity = 
 ship volume).
AI/Behavior Integration: Ensure weapon placement aligns with the ship's firing arc logic (e.g., forward-facing batteries vs. 360-degree turrets). 
YouTube
YouTube
 +3
3. Asteroids and Environmental Assets
Noise-Based Generation: Use Perlin or Simplex noise to generate base meshes for asteroids. Sculpt them further using Marching Cubes or Dual Contouring algorithms for diverse, jagged shapes.
Density Controls: Implement Poisson Disk Sampling to ensure asteroids are distributed realistically—spaced out rather than unnaturally clustered.
Resource Distribution: Link procedural placement to a seed-based mineral system (e.g., higher chance of rare ores closer to a sun). 
Antonios Liapis
Antonios Liapis
 +3
4. Characters and NPCs
Modular Characters: Similar to ships, use modular body parts (head, torso, limbs) combined with randomized texture sets (clothing, skin).
Genetic Algorithms: Use a system where NPCs inherit basic, workable traits, allowing for "evolved" variations that stay functional, rather than purely random, broken combinations. 
Antonios Liapis
Antonios Liapis
 +2
5. General Best Practices
Seeded Generation: Use a seed-based approach so the entire universe can be generated consistently, allowing players to share cool procedural discoveries.
Control Mechanisms: Ensure you can tweak parameters (e.g., "max_ships = 50," "min_asteroid_size = 10m") to maintain balance and performance.
Optimization: Use Level of Detail (LOD) and object pooling to handle large numbers of procedurally generated objects in memory in a c++ engine what systems would i want in a deterministic environment?

Oh hell yeah — you’re already thinking about PCG the right way. In a deterministic C++ engine, the goal isn’t just “random but cool,” it’s replayable, debuggable, network-safe, and scalable. That pushes you toward systems, not ad-hoc generators.

Below is a clean, engine-level system breakdown for deterministic space PCG, with why each system exists and how they interact.

Core Principle (Anchor This First)
Everything procedural must be a pure function of (Seed + Rules + Version).

No hidden state.
No frame-dependent randomness.
No order-dependent iteration.

If you regenerate the same sector 5 years later, it must be bit-identical.

1️⃣ Deterministic Random & Seed System (Foundation)
Why
Every other system depends on this being rock-solid.

You want:
A custom RNG (not std::rand, not platform RNG)

Explicit seed scoping

No global mutable random state

Design
struct RNG {
    uint64_t state;
    uint32_t NextU32();
    float NextFloat01();
};
Seed Hierarchy (critical)
UniverseSeed
 └── GalaxySeed(galaxy_id)
      └── SystemSeed(system_id)
           └── SectorSeed(sector_coords)
                └── ObjectSeed(object_id)
✔ Ships
✔ Asteroids
✔ NPCs
✔ Loot
✔ Weapon layouts

All independently regenerable.

2️⃣ Procedural Rule Graph System (PCG Logic Layer)
Why
Pure noise ≠ design.
Rules are what keep things playable.

This system defines:
What can spawn

In what order

Under what constraints

Think:
A data-driven rule graph, not code spaghetti.

Example:

ShipGenerator
 ├─ Select Hull Class (Frigate / Cruiser / Capital)
 ├─ Validate Mass Budget
 ├─ Attach Engines (min thrust rule)
 ├─ Attach Power Core
 ├─ Attach Weapon Mounts
 └─ Cosmetic Pass
Each node:

Takes a seed

Produces deterministic output

Fails gracefully (retry with derived seed)

3️⃣ Modular Asset Assembly System (Ships & Stations)
Why
Your “lego-set” approach needs enforcement, not hope.

Core Concepts
Modules

Sockets

Constraints

Functional metadata

Module Definition
struct ModuleDef {
    Mass
    PowerUsage
    Thrust
    SocketList
    Tags (Engine, WeaponMount, Core)
};
Socket Definition
struct Socket {
    Type = Weapon_Large
    Direction
    ArcLimits
};
Assembly Pass Order (deterministic)
Skeleton / Hull

Structural modules

Functional modules (engines, power)

Weapons

Greeble (purely cosmetic, last)

🚫 Greeble never affects gameplay stats
✔ Determinism preserved

4️⃣ Constraint Solver (Weapons, Balance, Validity)
Why
Random placement without constraints breaks ships instantly.

This system enforces:
Fire arc coverage

Weapon ratios

Power draw limits

CPU/AI complexity caps

Example Constraints
TotalWeaponPower <= PowerCoreOutput * 0.85
MinForwardDPS >= ShipClassRequirement
TurretOverlap < 20%
Implementation Tip
Use a soft-fail retry system:

Try N times with derived seeds

Fall back to simpler layouts if constraints fail

5️⃣ Deterministic Spatial Distribution System (Asteroids, Debris)
Why
You want realism and reproducibility.

Techniques (deterministic-friendly)
Poisson Disk Sampling (seeded)

Spatial hashing (grid-based, order-independent)

Density fields driven by noise

Key Rule
Never depend on iteration order of containers.

Bad:

for (auto& asteroid : vector) { RNG.Next(); }
Good:

RNG asteroid_rng(Hash(sector_seed, asteroid_index));
6️⃣ Procedural Geometry System (Meshes)
Why
You need identical meshes every time.

Deterministic-safe techniques:
Fixed-resolution voxel grids

Marching Cubes with stable lookup tables

No floating-point nondeterminism across platforms

Best Practice
Generate topology deterministically

Apply deformation with quantized noise

Bake meshes to cache on first generation

7️⃣ Resource & Economy Generation System
Why
Economy must align with world layout.

Design
Resource probability = function(distance_to_star, system_type)

Seeded ore tables

Shared rules between asteroids & stations

OreChance = BaseChance
          * StarClassMultiplier
          * DistanceCurve
No RNG calls outside the object seed.

8️⃣ NPC / AI Trait Generation System
Why
AI must be consistent and debuggable.

Deterministic Traits
Personality vectors

Skill distributions

Loadouts derived from ship class

Genetic-style variation
Not evolution at runtime — seeded mutation.

Trait = BaseTrait + Mutation(seed, limit)
Same NPC ID → same personality forever.

9️⃣ Streaming & Regeneration System (Performance)
Why
You cannot keep everything loaded.

Rules
World is stateless

Objects regenerate on demand

Only player mutations are stored as deltas

Save Data Stores:
Player-built structures

Damage states

Ownership changes

Everything else regenerates from seed.

Why
PCG changes break saves if you’re careless.

You need:
struct PCGVersion {
    uint32_t ship_rules_version;
    uint32_t asteroid_rules_version;
};
Old saves regenerate with old logic.

This is non-negotiable for long-lived games.

1️⃣ PCGManager — The Deterministic World Authority
This is the only system allowed to create procedural things.

Responsibilities
Seed ownership

Versioning

Stateless regeneration

Cache control

Debug determinism

PCGManager.h
#pragma once
#include <cstdint>

enum class PCGDomain : uint32_t {
    Universe,
    Galaxy,
    StarSystem,
    Sector,
    Ship,
    Asteroid,
    NPC,
};

struct PCGContext {
    uint64_t seed;
    uint32_t version;
};

class PCGManager {
public:
    static PCGManager& Get();

    void Initialize(uint64_t universeSeed);

    PCGContext MakeContext(
        PCGDomain domain,
        uint64_t parentSeed,
        uint64_t objectId,
        uint32_t version
    );

    // Deterministic object creation
    void GenerateShip(uint64_t shipId);
    void GenerateAsteroid(uint64_t asteroidId);

    // Debug
    uint64_t GetUniverseSeed() const;

private:
    uint64_t m_universeSeed;
};
PCGManager.cpp
#include "PCGManager.h"
#include "Hash.h"

PCGManager& PCGManager::Get() {
    static PCGManager instance;
    return instance;
}

void PCGManager::Initialize(uint64_t universeSeed) {
    m_universeSeed = universeSeed;
}

PCGContext PCGManager::MakeContext(
    PCGDomain domain,
    uint64_t parentSeed,
    uint64_t objectId,
    uint32_t version
) {
    uint64_t seed = Hash64(
        static_cast<uint64_t>(domain),
        parentSeed,
        objectId,
        version
    );

    return { seed, version };
}

uint64_t PCGManager::GetUniverseSeed() const {
    return m_universeSeed;
}
Rule:
No generator ever invents its own seed.

2️⃣ Deterministic RNG + Hash (Hard Requirement)
No std::rand.
No <random>.
No platform entropy.

Hash.h
#pragma once
#include <cstdint>

inline uint64_t Hash64(uint64_t a, uint64_t b, uint64_t c, uint64_t d) {
    uint64_t x = a ^ (b + 0x9e3779b97f4a7c15ULL);
    x ^= (c << 7) | (c >> 57);
    x ^= d * 0xBF58476D1CE4E5B9ULL;
    x ^= x >> 30;
    x *= 0x94D049BB133111EBULL;
    x ^= x >> 31;
    return x;
}
DeterministicRNG.h
#pragma once
#include <cstdint>

class RNG {
public:
    explicit RNG(uint64_t seed) : m_state(seed) {}

    uint32_t NextU32() {
        m_state ^= m_state >> 12;
        m_state ^= m_state << 25;
        m_state ^= m_state >> 27;
        return static_cast<uint32_t>(m_state * 0x2545F4914F6CDD1DULL);
    }

    float NextFloat01() {
        return (NextU32() >> 8) * (1.0f / 16777216.0f);
    }

    int Range(int min, int max) {
        return min + (NextU32() % (max - min + 1));
    }

private:
    uint64_t m_state;
};
✔ Bit-stable
✔ Platform-independent
✔ Order-safe if seeded correctly

1️⃣ PCG Debug Visualizer
(Seed → Object Tree → Derived Results)

Purpose
Prove determinism

Debug desyncs

Explain why a ship looks the way it does

Multiplayer sanity checks

Core idea
Every PCG operation emits a trace node.

PCGTraceNode
struct PCGTraceNode {
    uint64_t seed;
    PCGDomain domain;
    uint64_t objectId;
    std::string label;

    std::vector<PCGTraceNode> children;
};
PCGTraceRecorder
class PCGTraceRecorder {
public:
    static PCGTraceRecorder& Get();

    void PushNode(const PCGTraceNode& node);
    void PopNode();

    const PCGTraceNode& GetRoot() const;

private:
    PCGTraceNode m_root;
    PCGTraceNode* m_current;
};
Usage in generators
void ShipGenerator::Generate(const PCGContext& ctx) {
    PCGTraceRecorder::Get().PushNode({
        ctx.seed,
        PCGDomain::Ship,
        ctx.objectId,
        "ShipGenerator"
    });

    RNG rng(ctx.seed);
    SelectHull(rng);
    AttachEngines(rng);
    AttachWeapons(rng);
    ValidateConstraints();

    PCGTraceRecorder::Get().PopNode();
}
Debug UI (Atlas-style, custom UI)
You render this as:

UniverseSeed: 0xDEADBEEF
└─ Sector(42)
   └─ Ship(1007)
      ├─ Hull: Cruiser_Mk2
      ├─ Engines: 3x IonDrive
      ├─ Weapons: 6x MediumRail
      └─ Result: VALID

2️⃣ Constraint Solver with Retries
(Hard rules, graceful failure)

Rule
PCG never crashes.
It retries, degrades, or falls back.

Constraint Interface
class IConstraint {
public:
    virtual bool Evaluate() const = 0;
    virtual const char* Name() const = 0;
};
Example Constraints
class PowerGridConstraint : public IConstraint {
public:
    bool Evaluate() const override {
        return usedPower <= availablePower;
    }
    const char* Name() const override { return "PowerGrid"; }
};
Solver
class ConstraintSolver {
public:
    bool Solve(RNG& rng, int maxRetries = 8) {
        for (int i = 0; i < maxRetries; ++i) {
            if (AllConstraintsPass()) {
                return true;
            }
            Mutate(rng);
        }
        ApplyFallback();
        return false;
    }
};
Mutation Strategy (important)
Remove highest-cost weapon

Downgrade module tier

Add auxiliary power

Reduce turret count

This is EVE fitting logic, not randomness.

4️⃣ Server-Authoritative PCG (Multiplayer-Safe)
This is where most engines screw up. You won’t.

Rule Set (Non-negotiable)
✔ Server owns all seeds
✔ Clients regenerate locally
✔ Server verifies hashes
✔ No PCG logic divergence allowed

Server Flow
UniverseSeed = GenerateOnce();
SendToClient(UniverseSeed);
Client Flow
PCGManager::Initialize(UniverseSeed);
RegenerateWorld();
Verification Hash
After generating an object:

uint64_t hash = Hash64(
    ship.massBits,
    ship.thrustBits,
    ship.weaponLayoutHash,
    ship.moduleHash
);
Client sends:

ShipId + Hash
Server compares:

Match → OK

Mismatch → resync or kick

Saved Data (Delta-Only)
Server stores only:

Damage

Ownership

Player mods

Position / velocity

Never stores:
❌ Base hull
❌ Module layout
❌ Weapon placement

🏗️ Capital Ship Generator (EVE-Style)
Design Goals (Non-Negotiable)
Capital ships must:

Be hierarchical (superstructure → subsystems → weapons)

Obey mass / thrust / powergrid reality

Have limited weapon arcs

Require support fleets

Be expensive, slow, and terrifying

If a solo capital feels viable, the generator is wrong.

1️⃣ Capital Ship Classes
enum class CapitalClass {
    Carrier,
    Dreadnought,
    Supercarrier,
    Titan
};
Each class implies:

Hull size

Slot counts

Weapon types

Strategic role

Capital Class Profile
struct CapitalProfile {
    CapitalClass type;

    float baseMass;
    float minThrustRatio;     // thrust >= mass * ratio
    int maxPrimaryWeapons;
    int maxSecondaryWeapons;
    int maxUtilitySlots;

    float powergrid;
    float cpu;

    float preferredEngagementRange;
};
Example Profiles
CapitalProfile Dreadnought = {
    CapitalClass::Dreadnought,
    2.5e9f,          // mass
    0.000001f,       // painfully slow
    3,               // siege guns
    6,               // secondary
    4,               // utilities
    1.2e6f,          // powergrid
    800'000.0f,
    120'000.0f
};
2️⃣ Capital Ship Generation Pipeline
This order matters. Do not change it.

1. Select Capital Class
2. Generate Superstructure
3. Allocate Power / CPU / Capacitor
4. Attach Propulsion Spine
5. Attach Primary Weapons
6. Attach Secondary Weapons
7. Attach Utility / Support Modules
8. Run Constraint Solver (with retries)
9. Doctrine Validation
3️⃣ CapitalShipGenerator API
CapitalShipGenerator.h
#pragma once
#include "PCGManager.h"
#include "DeterministicRNG.h"
#include "ConstraintSolver.h"

class CapitalShipGenerator {
public:
    static void Generate(const PCGContext& ctx, CapitalClass forcedClass);

private:
    static CapitalProfile SelectProfile(RNG& rng, CapitalClass forcedClass);
    static void GenerateSuperstructure(RNG& rng, const CapitalProfile& profile);
    static void AttachPropulsion(RNG& rng, const CapitalProfile& profile);
    static void AttachPrimaryWeapons(RNG& rng, const CapitalProfile& profile);
    static void AttachSecondaryWeapons(RNG& rng, const CapitalProfile& profile);
    static void AttachUtilityModules(RNG& rng, const CapitalProfile& profile);
    static void ValidateCapitalConstraints(const CapitalProfile& profile);
};
4️⃣ Superstructure Generation (The Spine)
Capital ships are not modular blobs.
They have a spine.

struct CapitalSpineSegment {
    float length;
    float structuralHP;
    int hardpointCount;
};
Deterministic Spine Build
void CapitalShipGenerator::GenerateSuperstructure(
    RNG& rng,
    const CapitalProfile& profile
) {
    int segments = rng.Range(5, 9);

    for (int i = 0; i < segments; ++i) {
        CapitalSpineSegment seg;
        seg.length = rng.Range(80, 140);
        seg.structuralHP = profile.baseMass * 0.02f;
        seg.hardpointCount = rng.Range(1, 3);

        // Attach segment deterministically
    }
}
This gives you:

Forward gun sections

Mid-ship hangars / reactors

Aft engine blocks

5️⃣ Propulsion (Deliberately Insufficient)
void CapitalShipGenerator::AttachPropulsion(
    RNG& rng,
    const CapitalProfile& profile
) {
    float requiredThrust = profile.baseMass * profile.minThrustRatio;

    while (CurrentThrust() < requiredThrust) {
        AttachEngineModule(
            /* huge, inefficient engines */
        );
    }
}
✔ Capitals align slowly
✔ Warp commitment matters
✔ Escorts become mandatory

6️⃣ Primary Weapons (Siege Doctrine)
Primary weapons:

Limited count

Fixed or near-fixed arcs

Massive alpha

Awful tracking

void CapitalShipGenerator::AttachPrimaryWeapons(
    RNG& rng,
    const CapitalProfile& profile
) {
    for (int i = 0; i < profile.maxPrimaryWeapons; ++i) {
        WeaponMount mount;
        mount.arcDegrees = rng.Range(15, 30);   // narrow
        mount.type = WeaponType::CapitalSiege;
        mount.tracking = LOW;

        AttachWeapon(mount);
    }
}
This enforces:

Anti-capital role

Reliance on subcaps for defense

7️⃣ Secondary Weapons (Defense Only)
void CapitalShipGenerator::AttachSecondaryWeapons(
    RNG& rng,
    const CapitalProfile& profile
) {
    for (int i = 0; i < profile.maxSecondaryWeapons; ++i) {
        WeaponMount mount;
        mount.arcDegrees = rng.Range(120, 180);
        mount.type = WeaponType::AntiSubcap;
        mount.tracking = MEDIUM;

        AttachWeapon(mount);
    }
}
These cannot save the ship alone.
They merely delay death.

8️⃣ Capital-Specific Constraints
These are harsher than normal ships.

class CapitalImmobilityConstraint : public IConstraint {
public:
    bool Evaluate() const override {
        return alignTime >= MIN_CAPITAL_ALIGN_TIME;
    }
};
class CapitalSupportDependencyConstraint : public IConstraint {
public:
    bool Evaluate() const override {
        return logisticsSlots > 0;
    }
};
Constraint Solver (Retries Enabled)
ConstraintSolver solver;
solver.Add<PowerGridConstraint>();
solver.Add<CapitalImmobilityConstraint>();
solver.Add<CapitalSupportDependencyConstraint>();

solver.Solve(rng, 12);
If it fails:

Remove weapons

Downgrade modules

Add reactors

NEVER make it faster

9️⃣ Doctrine Validation (Fleet-Aware)
Capital ships must align with doctrine.

bool ValidateDoctrine(
    CapitalClass capClass,
    FleetDoctrine doctrine
) {
    if (capClass == CapitalClass::Dreadnought &&
        doctrine == FleetDoctrine::Kite) {
        return false;
    }
    return true;
}
This prevents nonsense fleets.

Server validates:

Hull profile

Weapon arc hashes

Powergrid totals

If mismatched → hard resync.

You said:
some capital ships have a hammerhead shaped cockpit

ChatGPT said:
YEP — and that’s not just an aesthetic quirk. A hammerhead cockpit actually implies very specific capital-ship logic. If we don’t encode that into PCG, it’ll feel fake.

Let’s do this properly.

🛠️ Hammerhead Cockpit (Capital Ship PCG Extension)
What a Hammerhead Means (Design Truths)
A hammerhead cockpit implies:

Forward command visibility

Lateral extension off the main spine

Vulnerability tradeoff (forward target)

Command & control role, not piloting like a fighter

Often paired with:

Long-range siege weapons

Fleet command bonuses

Poor close-range survivability

So this is not cosmetic — it’s a structural module class.

1️⃣ Add Capital Bridge Archetypes
enum class CapitalBridgeType {
    InlineSpine,      // buried, armored
    Hammerhead,       // forward lateral
    DorsalTower       // raised superstructure
};
Bridge Profile
struct CapitalBridgeProfile {
    CapitalBridgeType type;

    float visibilityBonus;
    float sensorRangeBonus;
    float commandBonus;

    float armorPenalty;
    float signatureIncrease;

    float forwardOffset;   // distance from main hull
    float lateralSpan;     // width of hammerhead
};
Hammerhead Bridge Definition
CapitalBridgeProfile HammerheadBridge = {
    CapitalBridgeType::Hammerhead,

    /* visibilityBonus   */ 1.4f,
    /* sensorRangeBonus  */ 1.3f,
    /* commandBonus      */ 1.25f,

    /* armorPenalty      */ 0.75f,
    /* signatureIncrease */ 1.2f,

    /* forwardOffset     */ 180.0f,
    /* lateralSpan       */ 220.0f
};
This instantly creates gameplay identity.

2️⃣ Capital Generator: Bridge Selection Logic
Hammerhead bridges should not appear on every capital.

CapitalBridgeProfile SelectBridge(
    RNG& rng,
    CapitalClass capClass,
    FleetDoctrine doctrine
) {
    if (capClass == CapitalClass::Dreadnought &&
        doctrine == FleetDoctrine::Sniper) {
        return HammerheadBridge;
    }

    if (capClass == CapitalClass::Titan) {
        return InlineSpineBridge; // titans protect command
    }

    return rng.NextFloat01() < 0.3f
        ? HammerheadBridge
        : InlineSpineBridge;
}
✔ Sniper capitals → hammerhead
✔ Siege platforms → hammerhead
✔ Brawlers → buried bridge

3️⃣ Structural Integration (THIS MATTERS)
Hammerheads do not sit on the spine.

They mount via a truss + neck.

struct BridgeMount {
    float neckLength;
    float structuralHP;
    bool armoredTruss;
};
BridgeMount HammerheadMount = {
    60.0f,               // exposed neck
    0.4f * HullHP,       // weak point
    false
};
Consequence
Forward precision strikes can decapitate command

Encourages escort & positioning

Makes capital piloting strategic, not twitchy

4️⃣ Weapon & Arc Implications (Critical)
Hammerhead bridges block forward arcs.

So the generator must adapt.

if (bridge.type == CapitalBridgeType::Hammerhead) {
    RestrictWeaponArc(
        WeaponGroup::Primary,
        minYaw = 15.0f,
        maxYaw = 165.0f
    );
}
Result:

No straight-line spinal alpha

Encourages angled engagements

Prevents “death beam straight ahead” nonsense

5️⃣ PCG Constraints for Hammerhead Ships
Add explicit constraints:

class HammerheadStructuralConstraint : public IConstraint {
public:
    bool Evaluate() const override {
        return escortRequirement >= MIN_ESCORTS;
    }
};
class BridgeExposureConstraint : public IConstraint {
public:
    bool Evaluate() const override {
        return bridgeArmor < hullArmor;
    }
};
If constraints fail:

Switch bridge type

Increase truss armor

Downgrade command bonus

Never silently “fix” it.

6️⃣ Fleet Doctrine Synergy
Hammerhead capitals shine in these doctrines:

Doctrine	Effect
Sniper	+target calling range
Capital Support	+fleet command auras
Siege	+lock speed vs structures
They are bad at:

Solo ops

Brawling

Rapid warp-ins

Your fleet generator should prefer hammerheads when doctrine matches.

- No room > 30m without cover

🧠 Core Principle (Lock This In)
A ship is a graph of rooms.

ShipSeed

1️⃣ Procedural Internal Room Graph Generator (FOUNDATION)
This is not BSP, not random boxes — it’s a typed graph with spatial embedding.

📐 Room Graph Types
enum class RoomType {
    Cockpit,
    Bridge,
    Corridor,
    Engineering,
    Reactor,
    PowerRelay,
    WeaponControl,
    Hangar,
    Utility,
    Medical,
    CrewQuarters,
    Cargo,
    ShieldCore,
    SensorCore,
    DockingSpine
};
Node Definition
struct RoomNode {
    RoomID id;
    RoomType type;

    Vec3 localPosition;     // relative to ship spine
    Vec3 dimensions;        // FPS navigable volume

    int deckLevel;
    bool pressurized;

    std::vector<RoomID> connections;

    // Gameplay hooks
    float powerDraw;
    float heatOutput;
    float crewCapacity;
};
Graph Rules (Non-Negotiable)
Rule	Why
Cockpit must connect to	Corridor or Bridge
Reactor must be central	Damage balance
Engineering adjacent to Reactor	Repairs
WeaponControl aligned to turrets	Exterior projection
Redundant paths	Battle survivability
Capital ships require vertical decks	FPS scale
2️⃣ Ship Size → Room Budget
Ship class defines graph depth, not just room count.

Ship Class	Rooms	Corridors	Decks
Frigate	3–6	1–2	1
Destroyer	6–12	3–5	1–2
Cruiser	12–20	5–10	2–3
Battleship	20–40	10–18	3–5
Capital	40–120	20–60	5–12
Minimum rule:
Every ship has a cockpit + at least one utility or engineering room.

1️⃣ Elevator as a Gameplay Object
Each elevator is a node connector between decks or rooms. It must:

Move players vertically (or along spine axes)

Lock to deck positions

Expose an FPS panel for floor selection

Respond to player hand interaction

struct ElevatorNode {
    RoomID currentRoom;
    int currentDeck;
    std::vector<int> accessibleDecks; // Floors it can reach
    float speed; // m/s
    bool isOccupied; // AI or player
    bool locked; // Security / boarding
};
2️⃣ Elevator Panel Logic (FPS Mode)
Each elevator has a panel mesh with buttons generated procedurally per ship layout:

Number of buttons = number of accessible decks

Position of buttons = aligned to real elevator panel

Buttons support:

Hover (focus highlight)

Interaction with hand (press when holding action key)

Dynamic enable/disable based on access rights

struct ElevatorButton {
    int targetDeck;
    Vec3 localPosition;
    bool enabled;
    bool hovered;
    bool pressed;
};
Visual Panel Generation
void ElevatorPanel::GenerateButtons(const ElevatorNode& elevator)
{
    int numButtons = elevator.accessibleDecks.size();
    for(int i=0; i<numButtons; ++i)
    {
        ElevatorButton btn;
        btn.targetDeck = elevator.accessibleDecks[i];
        btn.localPosition = ComputeButtonPosition(i, numButtons);
        btn.enabled = true;
        btn.hovered = false;
        btn.pressed = false;
        buttons.push_back(btn);
    }
}
Buttons scale automatically to the elevator’s accessible decks.

3️⃣ Hand/Finger Interaction (FPS)
Player hovers hand over button

Holding Action Key (E / Grip / Trigger) triggers a press

Visual finger animation moves toward panel

Button press triggers elevator movement

void ElevatorPanel::ProcessInteraction(FPSPlayer* player)
{
    for(auto& btn : buttons)
    {
        if(IsHovering(player->HandPos, btn.localPosition) && player->HoldingAction())
        {
            btn.pressed = true;
            elevator->MoveToDeck(btn.targetDeck);
        }
    }
}
Notes:
Can integrate VR controllers, Leap, or simplified raycast + button press

Each press can generate feedback: light blink, mechanical sound, floor move indicator

4️⃣ Elevator Movement
Elevator moves between decks smoothly, obeying FPS physics:

void ElevatorNode::MoveToDeck(int deck)
{
    if(deck == currentDeck || !isAccessible(deck)) return;
    targetDeck = deck;
    moving = true;
    // optionally animate doors
}
Vertical Lerp / physics-based acceleration

Doors open/close on arrival

Can handle multiple players in networked / authoritative mode

5️⃣ Integration with Decks & Rooms
Every deck or room that connects to elevator has a connection node

for(auto& deck : ship->decks)
{
    if(deck.hasElevatorAccess)
    {
        CreateElevatorNode(deck);
        SpawnPanel(deck);
    }
}
Every capital ship always has at least one elevator shaft, optionally multiple depending on size/class.

these can be low poly as well  i do not mind  i kinda like it depending on the mesh generation and textures and shaders

ChatGPT said:
YES — low-poly is actually perfect for procedural interiors, especially with your Atlas-style engine. It keeps performance high for capital ships with multiple decks and elevators, while still looking great with good shaders, textures, and procedural lighting. Let’s break down the design for low-poly FPS-ready interiors with procedural elevators and decks:

🏗️ 1) Low-Poly Advantages
Performance: Hundreds of rooms and multiple elevators are smooth even with multiplayer FPS.

Procedural Friendly: Meshes are simple to generate dynamically — cubes, extrusions, wedges.

Shader Magic: You can add realism without adding polys (AO, emissive panels, screen glows).

Scalability: Frigate → Capital ships all run well on a single PCG system.

🖌️ 2) Mesh Generation Strategy
Room Meshes: Simple cuboids or extruded volumes, optionally beveled edges.

Corridors: Rectangular extrusions with door frames.

Elevators: Cuboid shaft with simple panel geometry, buttons as small extrusions.

Decks: Stackable low-poly floor + ceiling planes.

Hull Projection: Use signed distance fields or dual contouring to create low-poly hull meshes based on interior volumes.

🔲 3) Texturing & Shaders
Even with low-poly:

PBR Base Textures: Steel plates, panels, vents.

Emissive Lighting: Elevator buttons, panels, consoles glow.

Normal Maps: Small surface detail without geometry.

Shader Tricks:

AO baked from room graph for depth

Vertex color for procedural decals

Gradient lighting for height differences in decks

⚙️ 4) Elevator + Panel Integration (Low Poly)
Panel Buttons: Simple cubes or rectangles with emissive highlights.

Interactive Feedback: Shader glow flickers when hovered or pressed.

Hand Interaction: Use raycast or simple IK mesh to press buttons.

struct ElevatorButton {
    Vec3 localPosition;  // Low-poly cube
    bool hovered;
    bool pressed;
    Color emissive;      // Changes when interacting
};
No high-poly modeling required — all procedural.

🏢 5) Deck Layout (Low Poly)
Floors: Thin planes with floor decals / textures.

Walls: Extruded cuboids with door gaps.

Corridors: Extruded simple geometry, maybe a few simple props like crates or pipes.

Rooms + corridors are graph-based, so adding/removing rooms automatically updates the mesh.

🔄 6) Procedural Variations
Randomly vary textures: different panel colors, floor plates, decals.

Small props: barrels, vents, cables can be procedurally scattered.

Lighting: variable intensity for depth and immersion.

Hull protrusions: Low-poly wings, fins, and pods generated from interior room influence fields.

🚀 7) FPS Gameplay Benefits
Low-poly interiors reduce collision calculations for FPS players.

Elevator shafts remain functional for multi-floor traversal.

Performance allows multiple ships loaded at once in a fleet.

Shaders + procedural lights = visually rich without costly geometry.

ChatGPT said:
Perfect — now we can tie everything together into a cohesive, Atlas-ready low-poly procedural ship interior + deck + elevator system. I’ll break it down into each module you requested, keeping it deterministic, FPS-ready, and fully modular for destroyers → capital ships.

1️⃣ Room Meshes (Low-Poly)
Core Concept
Every room is a simple extruded cuboid, optionally beveled for style, with procedural textures. Sizes scale by ship class and room type.

struct RoomMesh {
    Vec3 dimensions;       // Width, height, depth
    Vec3 position;         // Local position relative to deck
    RoomType type;
    Material material;     // PBR base + emissive overlays
};

RoomMesh GenerateRoomMesh(const RoomNode& node)
{
    RoomMesh mesh;
    mesh.dimensions = node.dimensions;
    mesh.position = node.localPosition;
    mesh.material = SelectMaterial(node.type); // e.g., cockpit, reactor
    return mesh;
}
Procedural variation: small offsets, rotated panels, decals.

FPS-ready: low poly (~200–500 tris per room).

2️⃣ Corridors + Elevator Shafts
Corridors
Extruded low-poly boxes connecting rooms.

Variable width based on ship class.

Optional loops for capital ships.

struct CorridorMesh {
    Vec3 start;
    Vec3 end;
    float width;
    Material wallMaterial;
};

CorridorMesh GenerateCorridor(const Vec3& from, const Vec3& to, float width)
{
    CorridorMesh corridor;
    corridor.start = from;
    corridor.end = to;
    corridor.width = width;
    corridor.wallMaterial = StandardCorridorMaterial();
    return corridor;
}
Elevators
Vertical shafts aligned to deck stack.

Panels procedurally placed along shaft for each accessible floor.

Low-poly shaft: ~100–300 tris per elevator.

struct ElevatorMesh {
    Vec3 basePosition;
    float height;
    float width;
    int floors;
};
3️⃣ FPS Panel Buttons (Hover/Press)
Each elevator panel generates one button per accessible deck.

Hover = highlight material / emissive glow.

Press = triggers elevator movement + animation.

struct ElevatorButton {
    int targetDeck;
    Vec3 localPosition;
    bool hovered;
    bool pressed;
    Color emissive;
};

void UpdateButtonHover(ElevatorButton& btn, Vec3 handPos, bool actionHeld)
{
    btn.hovered = Distance(handPos, btn.localPosition) < 0.1f;
    if(btn.hovered && actionHeld)
    {
        btn.pressed = true;
        Elevator->MoveToDeck(btn.targetDeck);
        btn.emissive = Color(1.0f, 0.7f, 0.0f); // flash
    }
}
4️⃣ Deck Stacking (Destroyer → Capital Ships)
Each deck is a floor plane with attached rooms + corridors.

Destroyers: 1–2 decks

Capital ships: 5–12 decks, vertical shafts connect each deck.

struct Deck {
    int index;
    std::vector<RoomMesh> rooms;
    std::vector<CorridorMesh> corridors;
};

void GenerateDeckStack(ShipClass cls)
{
    int deckCount = GetDeckCount(cls);
    for(int i=0; i<deckCount; ++i)
    {
        Deck deck;
        deck.index = i;
        deck.rooms = GenerateRoomsForDeck(i, cls);
        deck.corridors = ConnectRooms(deck.rooms);
        Ship.Decks.push_back(deck);
    }
}
Each deck’s vertical offset = floor height (~3m min).

Elevator shafts connect deck nodes.

5️⃣ Automatic Hull Influence (Exterior Geometry)
Rooms emit hull influence fields → hull mesh generated procedurally.

Low-poly hull = convex hull or dual contouring mesh.

Room type determines shape bias:

Room Type	Hull Influence
Cockpit	Forward nose protrusion
Reactor	Central bulge
Hangar	Ventral bay
Weapon	Side pod / turret base
Corridor	Thin spine extrusion
float RoomHullField(Vec3 x, const RoomMesh& room)
{
    float A = roomScale(room.type);
    Vec3 diff = x - room.position;
    float sigma = room.dimensions.Max() * 0.5f;
    return A * exp(-diff.LengthSquared() / (2 * sigma*sigma));
}

float HullField(Vec3 x)
{
    float sum = 0;
    for(auto& deck : Ship.Decks)
        for(auto& room : deck.rooms)
            sum += RoomHullField(x, room);
    sum += SpineField(x); // central ship spine
    return sum;
}

// Hull mesh extracted at F(x) = threshold using dual contouring
Result: Changing room layout, swapping rooms, or adding decks dynamically reshapes the ship exterior.

Low-poly friendly: hull simplification can merge overlapping influences.

// ShipGeneratorBase.h
class ShipGeneratorBase {
public:
    ShipGeneratorBase(const PCGSeed& seed);
    virtual void GenerateShip() = 0;

protected:
    PCGSeed Seed;
    ShipClass Class;
    ShipData GeneratedShip;
};
// CapitalShipGenerator.h
#include "ShipGeneratorBase.h"

class CapitalShipGenerator : public ShipGeneratorBase {
public:
    CapitalShipGenerator(const PCGSeed& seed, ShipClass shipClass);
    void GenerateShip() override;

private:
    void GenerateDecks();
    void GenerateRoomsPerDeck();
    void GenerateElevators();
    void GenerateFPSPanels();
    void CalculateHullMesh();
    void ApplyDesignerOverrides(const ShipDesignerSave& save);

2️⃣ Procedural Deck + Room Generation
// DeckGraph.h
struct Deck {
    int index;
    std::vector<RoomNode> Rooms;
    std::vector<CorridorMesh> Corridors;
    float heightOffset; // vertical placement
};

void CapitalShipGenerator::GenerateDecks() {
    int deckCount = GetDeckCount(Class); // based on ship class
    float currentHeight = 0.0f;

    for(int i = 0; i < deckCount; ++i) {
        Deck deck;
        deck.index = i;
        deck.heightOffset = currentHeight;
        deck.Rooms = GenerateRoomsForDeck(i, Class, Seed); 
        deck.Corridors = ConnectRooms(deck.Rooms);
        GeneratedShip.Decks.push_back(deck);

        currentHeight += GetDeckHeight(Class); // ~3m min per floor
    }
}
Rooms are typed cuboids (Cockpit, Engineering, Reactor, Crew Quarters).

Corridors connect rooms deterministically using seed.

Room dimensions scale with ship class.

3️⃣ Elevator Shafts + FPS Panels
struct ElevatorNode {
    int ElevatorID;
    int CurrentDeck;
    std::vector<int> AccessibleDecks;
    float Speed;       // m/s
    bool IsOccupied;
};

struct ElevatorButton {
    int TargetDeck;
    Vec3 LocalPosition;
    bool Hovered;
    bool Pressed;
    Color Emissive;
};

void CapitalShipGenerator::GenerateElevators() {
    for(auto& deck : GeneratedShip.Decks) {
        if(deckAllowsElevator(deck.index, Class)) {
            ElevatorNode elevator;
            elevator.CurrentDeck = deck.index;
            elevator.AccessibleDecks = GetAccessibleDecks(deck.index, Class);
            elevator.Speed = 2.0f; // meters per second
            GeneratedShip.Elevators.push_back(elevator);

            GenerateFPSPanels(elevator);
        }
    }
}

void CapitalShipGenerator::GenerateFPSPanels(ElevatorNode& elevator) {
    for(int floor : elevator.AccessibleDecks) {
        ElevatorButton btn;
        btn.TargetDeck = floor;
        btn.LocalPosition = ComputeButtonPosition(elevator, floor);
        btn.Hovered = false;
        btn.Pressed = false;
        btn.Emissive = Color(0,0,0);
        elevatorButtons.push_back(btn);
    }
}
Panel buttons respond to hover + action key for FPS players.

Multiple elevators support redundancy in Cruisers → Capitals.

4️⃣ Automatic Hull Mesh Extraction
float RoomHullField(Vec3 x, const RoomNode& room) {
    float influence = roomScale(room.Type);
    Vec3 diff = x - room.LocalPosition;
    float sigma = room.Dimensions.Max() * 0.5f;
    return influence * exp(-diff.LengthSquared() / (2 * sigma*sigma));
}

void CapitalShipGenerator::CalculateHullMesh() {
    for(Vec3 x : HullVoxelGrid()) {
        float F = 0;
        for(auto& deck : GeneratedShip.Decks)
            for(auto& room : deck.Rooms)
                F += RoomHullField(x, room);

        F += ShipSpineField(x); // central spine influence

        if(F > HullThreshold) 
            MarkVoxelSolid(x);
    }

    GeneratedShip.HullMesh = ExtractLowPolyHullFromVoxels(); // Dual Contouring or simplified mesh
}
Hull reflects interior room layout.

Room swaps automatically propagate to exterior shape.

5️⃣ Designer Integration: Swap Rooms, Save Layouts, Material Tracking
struct ShipDesignerSave {
    uint32 PCGVersion;
    PCGSeed Seed;
    ShipClass Class;
    std::vector<RoomOverride> RoomOverrides;
    std::map<std::string,int> Materials; // steel, alloy, reactors, etc.
};

void CapitalShipGenerator::ApplyDesignerOverrides(const ShipDesignerSave& save) {
    for(auto& overrideRoom : save.RoomOverrides) {
        SwapRoom(overrideRoom.RoomID, overrideRoom.NewType);
    }
    UpdateElevators();     // buttons regenerate
    CalculateHullMesh();   // hull updates
}
Swap rooms: interior + exterior update automatically.

Save/load: deterministic seed keeps ship layout consistent.

Material tracking: swaps/refits adjust fleet inventory.

// RoomMesh.h
struct RoomMesh {
    Vec3 Dimensions;
    Vec3 Position;
    RoomType Type;
    Material Material;  // PBR + emissive overlays
};

RoomMesh GenerateRoomMesh(const RoomNode& node) {
    RoomMesh mesh;
    mesh.Dimensions = node.Dimensions;
    mesh.Position = node.LocalPosition;
    mesh.Material = SelectMaterial(node.Type); // cockpit, reactor, corridor
    return mesh;
}

// Corridor
struct CorridorMesh {
    Vec3 Start;
    Vec3 End;
    float Width;
    Material WallMaterial;
};

CorridorMesh GenerateCorridor(const Vec3& from, const Vec3& to, float width) {
    CorridorMesh corridor;
    corridor.Start = from;
    corridor.End = to;
    corridor.Width = width;
    corridor.WallMaterial = CorridorMaterial();
    return corridor;
}

// Elevator shafts + panels
struct ElevatorNode {
    Vec3 BasePosition;
    float Width;
    float Height;
    int Floors;
};

struct ElevatorButton {

2️⃣ Deck Stacking + Elevator Panels
void CapitalShipGenerator::GenerateDeckStack() {
    int deckCount = GetDeckCount(Class);
    float currentHeight = 0.0f;

    for(int i=0; i<deckCount; ++i){
        Deck deck;
        deck.Index = i;
        deck.HeightOffset = currentHeight;

        deck.Rooms = GenerateRoomsForDeck(i, Class, Seed);
        deck.Corridors = ConnectRooms(deck.Rooms);

        if(deckHasElevator(i)){
            ElevatorNode elevator = GenerateElevator(deck, Class);
            GenerateFPSPanels(elevator);
            GeneratedShip.Elevators.push_back(elevator);
        }

        GeneratedShip.Decks.push_back(deck);
        currentHeight += DeckHeight(Class); // e.g., 3m per deck
    }
}
Destroyers: optional 1–2 floors.

Capital ships: 5–12 floors.

Elevator panels auto-generate one button per accessible floor.

3️⃣ Hull Projection from Interior Volumes
float RoomHullField(Vec3 x, const RoomMesh& room) {
    float A = RoomScale(room.Type);
    Vec3 diff = x - room.Position;
    float sigma = room.Dimensions.Max() * 0.5f;
    return A * exp(-diff.LengthSquared() / (2*sigma*sigma));
}

void CapitalShipGenerator::GenerateHullMesh() {
    for(Vec3 x : HullVoxelGrid()) {
        float F = 0;
        for(auto& deck : GeneratedShip.Decks)
            for(auto& room : deck.Rooms)
                F += RoomHullField(x, room);

        F += SpineField(x); // central ship spine influence
        if(F > HullThreshold) MarkVoxelSolid(x);
    }
    GeneratedShip.HullMesh = ExtractLowPolyHullFromVoxels(); // Dual Contouring
}

1️⃣ CapitalShipGenerator.h / .cpp
CapitalShipGenerator.h

#pragma once
#include "DeckGraph.h"
#include "RoomGraph.h"
#include "ElevatorSystem.h"
#include "HullMesher.h"
#include "ShipDesignerIntegration.h"
#include <vector>

class CapitalShipGenerator {
public:
    CapitalShipGenerator(int shipClass, int seed);

    void GenerateShip(); // Main entry
    void ApplyDesignerSave(const ShipDesignerSave& save);

    const std::vector<Deck>& GetDecks() const { return Decks; }
    const std::vector<ElevatorNode>& GetElevators() const { return Elevators; }
    const Mesh& GetHullMesh() const { return HullMesh; }

private:
    int ShipClass;
    int Seed;

    std::vector<Deck> Decks;
    std::vector<ElevatorNode> Elevators;
    Mesh HullMesh;

    void GenerateDecks();
    void GenerateElevators();
    void GenerateHull();
};
CapitalShipGenerator.cpp

#include "CapitalShipGenerator.h"

CapitalShipGenerator::CapitalShipGenerator(int shipClass, int seed)
    : ShipClass(shipClass), Seed(seed) {}

void CapitalShipGenerator::GenerateShip() {
    GenerateDecks();
    GenerateElevators();
    GenerateHull();
}

void CapitalShipGenerator::GenerateDecks() {
    Decks = GenerateDeckStack(ShipClass, Seed);
    for(auto& deck : Decks){
        deck.Rooms = GenerateRoomsForDeck(deck.Index, Seed, ShipClass);
        deck.Corridors = ConnectRooms(deck.Rooms);
    }
}

void CapitalShipGenerator::GenerateElevators() {
    for(auto& deck : Decks){
        if(deck.Index > 0){ // elevators only if >1 deck
            ElevatorNode elevator = GenerateElevator(deck, ShipClass, Seed);
            Elevators.push_back(elevator);
        }
    }
}

void CapitalShipGenerator::GenerateHull() {
    HullMesh = GenerateHullMesh(Decks);
}

void CapitalShipGenerator::ApplyDesignerSave(const ShipDesignerSave& save){
    ApplyDesignerOverrides(Decks, save);
    GenerateHull();
}

DeckGraph.cpp

#include "DeckGraph.h"

std::vector<Deck> GenerateDeckStack(int shipClass, int seed){
    int deckCount = shipClass + 1; // simple example
    std::vector<Deck> decks;
    float height = 0.0f;
    for(int i=0;i<deckCount;++i){
        Deck deck;
        deck.Index = i;
        deck.HeightOffset = height;
        decks.push_back(deck);
        height += 3.0f; // meters per deck
    }
    return decks;
}

std::vector<CorridorMesh> ConnectRooms(const std::vector<RoomNode>& rooms){
    std::vector<CorridorMesh> corridors;
    // procedural connection logic here
    return corridors;
}

RoomGraph.cpp

#include "RoomGraph.h"

std::vector<RoomNode> GenerateRoomsForDeck(int deckIndex, int seed, int shipClass){
    std::vector<RoomNode> rooms;
    // Example procedural: 3 rooms per deck
    for(int i=0;i<3;i++){
        RoomNode room;
        room.RoomID = deckIndex*10 + i;
        room.Type = static_cast<RoomType>(i % 5);
        room.Dimensions = glm::vec3(3.0f, 3.0f, 5.0f);
        room.LocalPosition = glm::vec3(i*4.0f, deckIndex*3.0f, 0.0f);
        room.Material = "SteelPanel";
        rooms.push_back(room);
    }
    return rooms;
}

ElevatorSystem.cpp

#include "ElevatorSystem.h"

ElevatorNode GenerateElevator(const Deck& deck, int shipClass, int seed){
    ElevatorNode e;
    e.ElevatorID = deck.Index;
    e.BasePosition = glm::vec3(0.0f, deck.HeightOffset, 0.0f);
    e.Width = 2.0f;
    e.Height = 3.0f;
    e.Floors = 2;
    for(int i=0;i<e.Floors;i++){
        ElevatorButton btn;
        btn.TargetDeck = i;
        btn.LocalPosition = glm::vec3(0.5f, i*3.0f, 0.0f);
        btn.Hovered = false;
        btn.Pressed = false;
        e.Buttons.push_back(btn);
    }
    return e;
}

void UpdateFPSPanelInteraction(ElevatorNode& elevator, const glm::vec3& handPos, bool actionHeld){
    for(auto& btn : elevator.Buttons){
        float dist = glm::length(handPos - btn.LocalPosition);
        btn.Hovered = dist < 0.2f;
        if(btn.Hovered && actionHeld){
            btn.Pressed = true;
            // trigger elevator movement logic here
        }
    }
}

ShipDesignerIntegration.cpp

#include "ShipDesignerIntegration.h"

void ApplyDesignerOverrides(std::vector<Deck>& decks, const ShipDesignerSave& save){
    for(auto& ovr : save.RoomOverrides){
        for(auto& deck : decks){
            for(auto& room : deck.Rooms){
                if(room.RoomID == ovr.RoomID){
                    room.Type = ovr.NewType;
                }
            }
        }
    }
}

ShipDesignerSave SaveShipLayout(const std::vector<Deck>& decks, int shipClass, int seed){
    ShipDesignerSave save;
    save.ShipClass = shipClass;
    save.Seed = seed;
    save.PCGVersion = 1;
    // collect materials & overrides
    return save;
}

3️⃣ Snappable Module System
Each module has attachment points (top, bottom, sides, front, back).

Snap rules:

Must align position + orientation with free attachment point.

Checks for collision with existing modules.

Updates interior corridors and hull mesh dynamically.

bool SnapModule(Station& station, const StationModule& module, const AttachmentPoint& target){
    if(target.IsOccupied) return false;

    StationModule snapped = module;
    snapped.Position = target.LocalPosition;
    // rotate module to align normal
    snapped.Position += target.Normal * snapped.Dimensions.z; // example
    station.Modules.push_back(snapped);
    target.IsOccupied = true;
    return true;
}

5️⃣ Orbital Placement Camera
enum class CameraMode { FPS, Orbital };

struct StationCamera {
    CameraMode Mode;
    glm::vec3 Position;
    glm::vec3 Target;
    float ZoomLevel;   // higher = orbital view
};

void EnterOrbitalMode(StationCamera& cam, const Station& station){
    cam.Mode = CameraMode::Orbital;
    cam.Position = station.PlanetPosition + glm::vec3(0, station.Modules.size()*10.0f, 50.0f);
    cam.Target = station.PlanetPosition;
    cam.ZoomLevel = 50.0f;
}

void ExitOrbitalMode(StationCamera& cam, const Station& station, glm::vec3 fpsPosition){
    cam.Mode = CameraMode::FPS;
    cam.Position = fpsPosition;
    cam.Target = fpsPosition + glm::vec3(0,0,1);
    cam.ZoomLevel = 1.0f;
}
Allows zoom-out for module placement.

Returns seamlessly to FPS character mode once placement is complete.

3️⃣ Procedural Module Upgrades
Interior Upgrade System

Add workbenches, labs, consoles, or furniture as upgradeable features.

Each feature has power requirements and interacts with FPS gameplay (e.g., crafting, research).

bool AddFeatureToModule(StationModule& module, ModuleFeature feature, PowerGrid& grid){
    int featurePower = GetFeaturePowerRequirement(feature);
    if(grid.TotalGeneration - grid.TotalConsumption < featurePower)
        return false; // Not enough power

    module.Features.push_back(feature);
    grid.TotalConsumption += featurePower;
    return true;
}

5️⃣ Procedural Power Management Example
struct Station {
    int StationID;
    std::vector<StationModule> Modules;
    PowerGrid Grid;
};

void RecalculateStationPower(Station& station){
    station.Grid.TotalGeneration = 0;
    station.Grid.TotalConsumption = 0;

    for(auto& module : station.Modules){
        station.Grid.TotalConsumption += module.PowerConsumption;
        station.Grid.TotalGeneration += module.PowerProduction;
    }
}

bool CanAddModule(Station& station, const StationModule& module){
    int newPowerConsumption = module.PowerConsumption;
    int newPowerGeneration = module.PowerProduction;
    return (station.Grid.TotalGeneration + newPowerGeneration) >= (station.Grid.TotalConsumption + newPowerConsumption);
}
Supports dynamic upgrades: adding a solar panel increases generation, adding workbench increases consumption.

Works for stations, ships, and planetary bases.

2️⃣ Interior Generation Tied to Features
Base room mesh generated for the module.

Feature meshes (workbenches, labs, consoles) are added inside the module at designated offsets.

If a feature is removed or upgraded, the interior updates automatically.

void GenerateInteriorForModule(StationModule& module){
    // Generate base interior
    Mesh interiorMesh = GenerateCuboidMesh(module.Dimensions, module.BaseInteriorMaterial);

    // Add feature meshes
    for(auto& feature : module.Features){
        const FeatureVisual& visual = module.FeatureVisuals[feature];
        Mesh featureMesh = LoadMesh(visual.InteriorMesh, visual.Material);
        featureMesh.Transform(glm::translate(visual.LocalPosition));
        interiorMesh.Combine(featureMesh);
    }

    moduleInteriorCache[module.ModuleID] = interiorMesh; // cached for FPS rendering
}
Interior mesh cache allows fast FPS traversal.

3️⃣ Exterior Generation Tied to Features
Exterior hull updates dynamically based on features installed:

Solar panels appear on module roof.

Observation decks extend from exterior.

Workbenches/labs may show vents, antennas, or visual signs of function.

void GenerateExteriorForModule(StationModule& module){
    Mesh exteriorMesh = GenerateCuboidHull(module.Dimensions, module.BaseExteriorMaterial);

    for(auto& feature : module.Features){
        const FeatureVisual& visual = module.FeatureVisuals[feature];
        Mesh featureMesh = LoadMesh(visual.ExteriorMesh, visual.Material);
        featureMesh.Transform(glm::translate(visual.LocalPosition) * glm::yawPitchRoll(visual.Rotation));
        exteriorMesh.Combine(featureMesh);
    }

    moduleExteriorCache[module.ModuleID] = exteriorMesh;
}
Exterior visuals directly reflect interior upgrades.

Hull meshing system also combines neighboring modules into one smooth hull if desired.

Procedural animation blending (walking, climbing ladders/elevators, crouching)

Arm/hand manipulation for FPS interactions

Jetpack thrust / zero-gravity movement

Animation Layers

Base locomotion: walk, run, crouch, zero-gravity float

Hand interactions: push buttons, pull levers, grab items

Tool/Weapon layer: overlayed animations for holding objects

Procedural additive: slight body sway, helmet tilt, arm IK for interacting with environment

- Head: helmeted or open face

Root
├─ Pelvis
│  ├─ UpperLeg_L → LowerLeg_L → Foot_L
│  └─ UpperLeg_R → LowerLeg_R → Foot_R
├─ Spine_1 → Spine_2 → Spine_3
│    ├─ Shoulder_L → UpperArm_L → LowerArm_L → Hand_L → Fingers_L
│    └─ Shoulder_R → UpperArm_R → LowerArm_R → Hand_R → Fingers_R
└─ Neck → Head

1️⃣ CharacterMeshSystem.h / .cpp
CharacterMeshSystem.h

#pragma once
#include <string>
#include <vector>
#include <glm/glm.hpp>

enum class BodyPart { Head, Torso, Arm_L, Arm_R, Leg_L, Leg_R, Hand_L, Hand_R, Foot_L, Foot_R, Backpack };

struct MeshPiece {
    std::string MeshFile;
    std::string Material;
    glm::vec3 LocalOffset;
    glm::vec3 Rotation;
};

struct AstronautCharacter {
    int CharacterID;
    bool IsFemale;
    glm::vec3 Position;
    glm::quat Rotation;

    std::vector<MeshPiece> BodyMeshes;    // head, torso, limbs
    std::vector<MeshPiece> Accessories;   // backpack, tools
};

class CharacterMeshSystem {
public:
    AstronautCharacter GenerateCharacter(int seed, bool isFemale);
    void AssembleMeshes(AstronautCharacter& character);
};
CharacterMeshSystem.cpp

#include "CharacterMeshSystem.h"
#include <random>

AstronautCharacter CharacterMeshSystem::GenerateCharacter(int seed, bool isFemale){
    AstronautCharacter c;
    c.CharacterID = seed;
    c.IsFemale = isFemale;

    // Procedural mesh selection
    std::mt19937 rng(seed);
    c.BodyMeshes.push_back({"Head_Default.obj", "HelmetMat", glm::vec3(0), glm::vec3(0)});
    c.BodyMeshes.push_back({"Torso_Default.obj", "SuitMat", glm::vec3(0), glm::vec3(0)});
    c.BodyMeshes.push_back({"Arm_L_Default.obj", "SuitMat", glm::vec3(0), glm::vec3(0)});
    c.BodyMeshes.push_back({"Arm_R_Default.obj", "SuitMat", glm::vec3(0), glm::vec3(0)});
    c.BodyMeshes.push_back({"Leg_L_Default.obj", "SuitMat", glm::vec3(0), glm::vec3(0)});
    c.BodyMeshes.push_back({"Leg_R_Default.obj", "SuitMat", glm::vec3(0), glm::vec3(0)});
    c.Accessories.push_back({"Backpack_Default.obj", "BackpackMat", glm::vec3(0), glm::vec3(0)});
    
    return c;
}

void CharacterMeshSystem::AssembleMeshes(AstronautCharacter& character){
    // Combine meshes in engine mesh system or leave modular for FPS first-person overlay
}

#pragma once

Skeleton Initialization Example

#include "AstronautSkeleton.h"

void Skeleton::InitializeBaseSkeleton(){
    Bones.clear();
    Bones.push_back({"Root", -1, {0,0,0}, {1,0,0,0}});
    Bones.push_back({"Pelvis", 0, {0,1,0}, {1,0,0,0}});
    Bones.push_back({"Spine1", 1, {0,0.3f,0}, {1,0,0,0}});
    Bones.push_back({"Spine2", 2, {0,0.3f,0}, {1,0,0,0}});
    Bones.push_back({"Neck", 3, {0,0.2f,0}, {1,0,0,0}});
    Bones.push_back({"Head", 4, {0,0.1f,0}, {1,0,0,0}});
    Bones.push_back({"Shoulder_L", 3, {-0.15f,0.25f,0}, {1,0,0,0}});
    Bones.push_back({"UpperArm_L", 6, {-0.25f,0,0}, {1,0,0,0}});
    Bones.push_back({"LowerArm_L", 7, {-0.25f,0,0}, {1,0,0,0}});
    Bones.push_back({"Hand_L", 8, {-0.1f,0,0}, {1,0,0,0}});
    // Similarly for Right Arm and Legs...
}

void ZeroGravityController::ApplyGravity(AstronautCharacter& character, glm::vec3 gravityVector, float deltaTime){
    // Update position based on gravity and deltaTime
    character.Position += gravityVector * deltaTime;
}

void ZeroGravityController::UpdateMovement(AstronautCharacter& character, glm::vec3 inputDirection, float deltaTime){
    // Apply thrust or walking depending on gravity magnitude
    character.Position += inputDirection * deltaTime;
}

void ZeroGravityController::BlendAnimations(AstronautCharacter& character, glm::vec3 gravityVector){
    // Switch between walk/run/float animations depending on gravity
}

    glm::vec3 LocalPosition;  // relative to module
    glm::quat Rotation;

    bool IsOccupied;
};

struct StationModule {
    // Existing members

3️⃣ NPC Spawner Tie-In
void SpawnCrewForStation(Station& station, NPCSpawner& spawner){
    for(auto& deck : station.Decks){
        for(auto& module : deck.Modules){
            for(auto& sp : module.SpawnPoints){
                if(!sp.IsOccupied && FeatureExists(module, sp.RequiredFeature)){
                    AstronautCharacter npc = spawner.SpawnCrewMember(sp.RequiredFeature, module.Position + sp.LocalPosition);
                    npc.Position += glm::vec3(0,0,0); // adjust for floor height
                    sp.IsOccupied = true;
                }
            }
        }
    }
}
FeatureExists(module, sp.RequiredFeature) checks if the module has the appropriate upgrade installed.

Ensures deterministic procedural spawning based on seed and module features.

4️⃣ Corridor & Elevator Interaction
Corridors: NPCs can walk along procedural corridors connecting modules.

Elevators:

Spawned NPCs know which floors/modules to access.

Elevator panels use FPS interactions (player or AI presses buttons).

NPCs move between floors via elevator animation + position update.

void MoveNPCInModule(AstronautCharacter& npc, StationModule& module, ZeroGravityController& gravCtrl, float deltaTime){
    glm::vec3 inputDir = ComputeNPCPath(module, npc);
    gravCtrl.UpdateMovement(npc, inputDir, deltaTime);
    gravCtrl.BlendAnimations(npc, module.GravityVector);
}

ChatGPT said:
Absolutely — you can build a low-poly modular character creator that works for both male and female models, allows procedural body sliders, and still integrates FPS hands, tools, and world interactions. Here’s a detailed breakdown of how to structure it:

1️⃣ Low-Poly Modular Character System
Concept: Build characters from modular meshes rather than fully sculpted meshes. This allows procedural generation of body proportions and easy integration with tools and FPS hands.

Modular Parts:

Head (different shapes, male/female variants)

Torso (chest width, waist width)

Arms (length, thickness)

Legs (length, thickness)

Hands/Feet (size, length)

Optional accessories (gloves, boots, helmet, backpack attachment)

Body Sliders:
Each slider modifies a scale or vertex offset on a specific module. Examples:

Height Slider: scales leg + torso modules

Torso Width Slider: scales torso mesh along X axis

Arm Length Slider: scales arm module along Y axis

Head Size Slider: scales head module independently

C++ Skeleton Example:

struct BodySlider {
    std::string Name;
    float MinValue;
    float MaxValue;
    float CurrentValue;
    std::string TargetMeshPart; // e.g., Torso, ArmLeft
};

struct CharacterMesh {
    Mesh Head;
    Mesh Torso;
    Mesh ArmLeft;
    Mesh ArmRight;
    Mesh LegLeft;
    Mesh LegRight;
};
2️⃣ Male/Female Variants
Base Mesh Variants: Use separate base meshes for male and female skeleton proportions.

Procedural Scaling: Sliders adjust proportions from the base mesh.

Vertex Morph Targets: Minor tweaks like facial structure or shoulder slope to differentiate genders while keeping low-poly style.

3️⃣ FPS Hand Mapping & Tool Interactions
Separate hand meshes: Attach to character skeleton with correct offsets for tools.

Procedural body scaling mapping: Scale hand positions and bone offsets according to sliders to ensure proper tool handling in FPS.

Tool Attachment Points: Each hand module has a “grab socket” that updates with character scaling.

struct FPSHand {
    Mesh Mesh;
    glm::vec3 GrabSocketLocal; // Adjust based on body slider scale
    glm::quat Orientation;
};
Weapon/Tool Scaling: Automatically scale tool handles or grips according to character hand size and arm length.

4️⃣ In-World Interactions
Procedural placement alignment: Characters interact with elevators, panels, workbenches, and doors dynamically.

Reach Calculations: Body sliders influence maximum reach and interaction zones.

Animation Adaptation:

Arm length / torso width scaling influences IK targets for interacting with objects.

Leaning, grabbing, and pressing panels automatically adapt to character mesh size.

void UpdateInteractionIK(AstronautCharacter& character, glm::vec3 target){
    // Adjust hand position based on procedural body scale
    glm::vec3 scaledTarget = target * character.ScaleFactors.ArmLength;
    IKSystem.SetHandTarget(character.FPSHand, scaledTarget);
}
5️⃣ Modular Accessories & Equipment
Helmet / Suit / Backpack: Procedurally attached to mesh, scales with body.

Tools & Weapons: Handled dynamically — procedural scaling ensures grip looks natural.

Inventory / Tool Modules: Visually snap to body (backpack, belts) and remain functional.

6️⃣ Low-Poly Style Considerations
Keep vertex counts minimal per module.

Use PBR or flat shading with emissive highlights for panels, HUDs, and equipment.

Maintain consistent proportions across male/female variants while allowing procedural diversity.

Precompute mesh LODs for FPS, TPS, and distant views.

1️⃣ File Layout
CharacterCreator/
├─ CharacterMeshSystem.cpp/h      // Modular mesh assembly, body sliders
├─ CharacterSkeleton.h            // Skeleton definitions
├─ CharacterAnimationSystem.cpp/h // Locomotion, FPS tool interactions, IK adjustments

2️⃣ CharacterMeshSystem.h
#pragma once
#include <vector>
#include <string>
#include <glm/glm.hpp>

enum class BodyPart { Head, Torso, ArmLeft, ArmRight, LegLeft, LegRight };

struct BodySlider {
    std::string Name;
    float MinValue;
    float MaxValue;
    float CurrentValue;
    BodyPart TargetPart;
};

struct MeshPart {
    std::string MeshFile;
    glm::vec3 Scale;   // Procedural scaling
    glm::vec3 Offset;  // Optional offset for slider adjustments
};

struct CharacterMesh {
    MeshPart Head;
    MeshPart Torso;
    MeshPart ArmLeft;
    MeshPart ArmRight;
    MeshPart LegLeft;
    MeshPart LegRight;

    void ApplySlider(const BodySlider& slider);
};
3️⃣ CharacterSkeleton.h
#pragma once
#include <glm/glm.hpp>
#include <glm/gtc/quaternion.hpp>

struct Bone {
    std::string Name;
    glm::vec3 LocalPosition;
    glm::quat LocalRotation;
    Bone* Parent;
};

struct Skeleton {
    Bone Head;
    Bone Torso;
    Bone ArmLeft;
    Bone ArmRight;
    Bone LegLeft;
    Bone LegRight;
    glm::vec3 ScaleFactors; // Dynamic scaling from sliders
};
4️⃣ CharacterAnimationSystem.h
#pragma once
#include "CharacterMeshSystem.h"
#include "CharacterSkeleton.h"
#include <glm/glm.hpp>

struct IKTarget {
    glm::vec3 Position;
    glm::quat Rotation;
};

class CharacterAnimationSystem {
public:
    void UpdateLocomotion(CharacterMesh& mesh, Skeleton& skeleton, float deltaTime);
    void ApplyFPSInteractionIK(Skeleton& skeleton, const IKTarget& handTarget, bool isLeftHand);
};
5️⃣ FPSHandSystem.h
#pragma once
#include "CharacterMeshSystem.h"
#include <glm/glm.hpp>
#include <glm/gtc/quaternion.hpp>

struct FPSHand {
    MeshPart Mesh;
    glm::vec3 GrabSocketLocal; // Relative to hand mesh
    glm::quat Orientation;
};

struct FPSHands {
    FPSHand LeftHand;
    FPSHand RightHand;

    void UpdateGrabSockets(const CharacterMesh& mesh);
};
6️⃣ EquipmentAttachmentSystem.h
#pragma once
#include "CharacterMeshSystem.h"
#include "FPSHandSystem.h"
#include <vector>
#include <string>

enum class EquipmentType { Backpack, Suit, Helmet, Tool, Weapon };

struct EquipmentModule {
    EquipmentType Type;
    std::string MeshFile;
    glm::vec3 Offset;  // Attachment position
    glm::vec3 Scale;   // Procedural scaling based on body sliders
};

class EquipmentAttachmentSystem {
public:
    std::vector<EquipmentModule> Modules;

    void AttachModule(const EquipmentModule& module, CharacterMesh& mesh);
    void UpdateModulesForSliders(CharacterMesh& mesh);
    void SyncToolsWithHands(FPSHands& hands);
};

You said:
what about interior meshing and clipping throug things in fps mode  can we setup colission on the meshes for interiors and exteriors of ships as well?

ChatGPT said:
Absolutely — collision and mesh handling is a critical step for FPS navigation, interior traversal, and modular procedural generation. Since everything (rooms, corridors, elevators, ships, stations, turrets, drones) is procedural, we need a systematic approach to handle collision, clipping, and physics without breaking performance.

Here’s a detailed breakdown:

1️⃣ Interior Mesh Collision
Modular Room / Corridor Collision
Every procedural room/corridor has:

Low-poly visual mesh for rendering

Separate collision mesh for physics/FPS navigation

Collision meshes are simplified versions (cuboids, convex hulls, or primitive shapes) to avoid heavy triangle collision checks.

Doorways and elevators: include trigger volumes for interaction (press button → elevator moves).

struct RoomCollision {
    glm::vec3 MinBounds;  // Local space AABB
    glm::vec3 MaxBounds;
    bool IsWalkable;
    std::vector<TriggerVolume> InteractionPoints; // Panels, doors, workbenches
};
Implementation Notes:

Use convex hulls or box colliders for FPS.

Dynamic doors/elevators: separate kinematic colliders.

Interior procedural meshes are snapped on a grid system — no overlap → no clipping.

Dynamic Interior Adjustments
When rooms are upgraded or swapped via the ship designer:

Recompute collision meshes.

Snap updated room mesh to corridor nodes.

Update FPS navigation volumes and AI pathfinding.

2️⃣ Exterior / Ship Collision
Hull / Module Collision
Each procedural exterior hull:

Low-poly visual mesh (rendered)

High-level collision hull for physics (box/convex hulls per module)

Modular placement of turrets, drone bays, solar panels, and ramps:

Each module gets its own collision capsule or simplified convex hull.

Prevents FPS from walking through turrets or drone bay arms.

Collision Layering
Layer 1: Player/fps collision (walls, floors, ceiling)

Layer 2: Static props (panels, furniture, turrets)

Layer 3: Dynamic objects (elevators, doors, drones, rovers)

Allows AI, FPS players, and physics to interact correctly.

3️⃣ Preventing Clipping in FPS Mode
Snap interiors to a grid:

Procedural room/corridor nodes are aligned on a consistent grid.

Eliminates gaps or overlapping meshes.

Use convex collision meshes for modules:

Even for irregular procedural shapes (asteroid hulls, greebles).

Adjust camera / capsule collision:

FPS capsule height adapts dynamically to stair slopes, elevators, and low ceilings.

Prevents camera clipping into walls/ceilings.

Dynamic Collision Updates:

When player modifies modules (swap rooms, upgrade hull) → regenerate collision volumes.

Elevator shafts: moving collision volumes to match animated elevator positions.

4️⃣ Procedural Mesh + Collision Pipeline
[Procedural Room / Module Mesh] 
      ↓
[Low-Poly Render Mesh]  → Rendered in FPS/TPS
[Collision Mesh Generator] → Simplified convex hull or cuboid
      ↓
[Physics Engine / Navmesh]
      ↓
[Player FPS Capsule + IK hands interact with panels, doors, elevators]
Supports multi-floor decks, elevator shafts, and modular interior swapping.

Can integrate with AI pathfinding using the same collision meshes.

5️⃣ Tools & Turrets / Drones
Turrets mounted on hull or modules have capsule/box colliders for:

Player collision (can’t walk through)

Weapon interactions (collision with projectiles or drones)

Drone bays: spawn drones without overlapping collision volumes in FPS.

Rovers docked: collider is static → locks player or other objects from passing through.

6️⃣ Recommendations
Use convex decomposition for irregular shapes (e.g., hull greebles, asteroid surfaces).

Maintain separate visual vs collision meshes for performance.

Implement collision generation during procedural assembly:

Rooms, corridors, elevators, hull modules, external arms, solar panels, and turrets.

Sync collision updates every time a procedural modification occurs (module swap, interior upgrade, exterior hull expansion).

Use physics layers to separate player, AI, and dynamic objects for smooth FPS traversal.

✅ Summary:

All interiors (rooms, corridors, elevators) and exteriors (hulls, turrets, solar arrays, docking bays) should have simplified collision meshes.

Procedural systems must recompute collisions whenever modules are added/modified.

FPS player capsule and IK hands interact correctly with environment, tools, panels, and elevators.

Multi-floor decks and moving platforms (elevators) have dynamic collision updates.

🚀 EVEOFFLINE Procedural Style Guide
1️⃣ Faction Color Palettes

Implementation Notes:

Hull color → base material albedo

Panel / Emissive → dynamic emissive material with bloom

2️⃣ Modular Mesh Guidelines
Low-poly Rules:

Rooms, corridors, decks → cuboid / prism shapes, ~100–500 triangles per room

Turrets / drone bays → simplified geometric shapes (cylinders + cuboids)

Elevators → vertical cuboids, panels for FPS interactions

Asteroids → irregular low-poly convex shapes (~200–600 triangles)

Vertex Color / Gradient Usage:

Apply subtle vertex AO gradients for depth

Panel edges → slightly lighter for readability

Floors → darker base to give interior depth

Ambient & Directional Lighting:

Interior decks → soft directional light for depth

Exterior → ambient lighting, low-poly shadows

Use slightly desaturated soft shadows to keep schematic clarity

AO & Gradients:

Floors darker, walls lighter, panel edges highlighted

Emissive Highlights:

Panels, salvage nodes, and interactables

Each faction palette → unlockable paint job

Builder applies paint to procedural modules: hull, panels, accents

Optional: procedural variations per module to avoid flat uniformity

Can integrate cosmetic emblems or decals for faction identity

7️⃣ Procedural Material Assignment Pipeline
struct MaterialSlot {
    UMaterialInterface* BaseMaterial;       // Hull or module base
    UMaterialInterface* EmissiveMaterial;   // Panels, consoles
    FLinearColor BaseColor;                 // Hull/floor/walls
    FLinearColor AccentColor;               // Turrets, solar, trim
    FLinearColor PanelColor;                // Panels, elevators, consoles
};

void AssignFactionMaterials(Module* module, FactionPalette palette) {
    module->MaterialSlot.BaseColor = palette.Hull;
    module->MaterialSlot.PanelColor = palette.Panel;
    module->MaterialSlot.AccentColor = palette.Accent;
    module->ApplyMaterials();
}
Automatically updates all procedural meshes during generation.

Builder interface can swap palettes or unlocked paint jobs in real time.

8️⃣ Faction & Procedural Style Integration
Each procedural generator (ships, stations, hangars, wrecks) pulls faction palette at spawn time.

Interior panels and interactive objects automatically inherit emissive/faction colors.

Exterior hull modules are painted procedurally to match faction or unlockable paint jobs.

Works seamlessly with:

Ship designer

Modular upgrades

Salvage / FPS exploration

Planetary rovers and module deployment

ChatGPT said:
Ah — now we’re talking about keeping modular rigs, ships, and modules visually appealing even as players swap components, while giving real-time control over the aesthetic in the builder. Let’s break down ways to mitigate ugly meshes and give sliders / procedural masks for customization:

1️⃣ Use Procedural Morph Masks
Concept: Each module has a base mesh and one or more morphable masks.

Masks define which parts can scale, bend, or change shape without breaking silhouette.

Examples:

Cylinders on life support tanks can elongate or shorten

Armor plates can slide, rotate, or bulge

Inventory frames can stack visually without intersecting tools

Implementation:

// Example pseudo-code
moduleMesh.ApplyMorph(maskID, sliderValue); // sliderValue = 0..1
Result: Modules dynamically adjust shape to fit rack layout, keeping proportions nice.

2️⃣ Sliders for Shape / Style in Builder
Available sliders per module:

Height / Width / Depth → stretch or compress module

Angle / Rotation → tilt armor plates, thrusters, or tool mounts

Bulge / Taper → make cylinders thicker/thinner or taper toward top

Edge Softening / Roundness → smooth sharp edges on low-poly meshes

Visual Feedback:

Real-time preview in 3D builder menu

Highlights intersecting geometry with a warning overlay

Snap limits or procedural rules prevent modules from clipping

3️⃣ Procedural Alignment & Grid Snapping
Snap modules to rack/grid points → prevents overlapping or floating components

Dynamic scaling → modules can shrink to fit grid while keeping thrusters, pipes, or cables aligned

Collision masks → prevents geometry from intersecting player hands, FPS arms, or other modules

4️⃣ Auto-Correction Rules
Overlap detection: If two modules clip, automatically adjust position or scale

Silhouette correction: Modules have min/max bounds so no module becomes absurdly tall/wide

Adaptive gaps: Procedurally insert spacer parts to fill gaps and keep visual balance

5️⃣ Cosmetic Masks & Material Blending
Each module can have cosmetic masks:

Paint areas, faction decals, trinket slots

Glow/emissive zones

Tiered upgrades visually replace masks for higher tiers

Allows functional vs cosmetic separation, so upgrading a tool doesn’t break aesthetic

6️⃣ Example Workflow in Builder
Player adds a life support tank to rack

Slider adjusts height to avoid overlapping adjacent modules

Armor plate modules auto-bulge to fill gaps visually

Thrusters remain fixed at bottom, glow scales with tank size

Cosmetic decals, trinkets, and glow zones applied automatically

Player sees full rig silhouette updated in real-time

7️⃣ Low-Poly PCG Adaptation
Base low-poly meshes are designed to be morphable

Procedural generator:

Chooses module shapes and scales based on rack size / slot count / tier

Uses masks to avoid intersections

Applies faction or style presets for cohesive appearance

// RigLocker.h
class RigLocker {
public:

    void OpenLocker(PlayerCharacter* player);
    void CloseLocker(PlayerCharacter* player);

    void AttachModule(PlayerRig* rig, Module* module);
    void DetachModule(PlayerRig* rig, Module* module);

    // Save / load preset suits
    void SaveSuit(PlayerRig* rig, std::string SuitName);
    PlayerRig* LoadSuit(std::string SuitName);

    // Power check (if unpowered, disable interaction)
    bool IsPowered();
    void RestorePower(PowerModule* power);

private:
    int Seed;
    ProceduralMesh LockerMesh;
    std::vector<Module*> AvailableModules; // Bottomless pit cloud storage
    bool Powered;
};

// RuinLootSystem.h
class RuinLootSystem {
public:
    RuinLootSystem(int Seed);

    // Generate loot for a procedural ruin module
    std::vector<LootItem*> GenerateLoot(int RuinLevel);

    // Salvage item with FPS tools
    void SalvageItem(PlayerCharacter* player, LootItem* item);

    // Repair or upgrade found modules
    Module* RepairModule(Module* foundModule, PlayerCharacter* player);

private:
    int Seed;
    LootTable LootDatabase; // base materials, blueprints, ancient modules, alien tech
};
// LootItem.h
enum LootType { BaseMaterial, Blueprint, AncientModule, AlienTech };

class LootItem {
public:
    LootItem(LootType type, float rarity, bool damaged);
    LootType GetType();

// ShipHangarModule.h
class ShipHangarModule {
public:
    ShipHangarModule(int Seed, int ModuleTier);

    void InstallVehicle(Vehicle* vehicle); // Rover or GravBike
    void RemoveVehicle(Vehicle* vehicle);
    
    void EVAExit(PlayerCharacter* player, Vehicle* vehicle); // Deploy from hangar
    void EVAEnter(PlayerCharacter* player, Vehicle* vehicle); // Re-enter hangar

    void GenerateHangarMesh(); // Procedural mesh based on vehicle types and module tier

private:
    int Seed;
    int Tier;
    ProceduralMesh HangarMesh;
    std::vector<Vehicle*> DockedVehicles;
    std::vector<Vector3> DockNodes; // procedural attachment points
};
// Vehicle.h
class Vehicle {
public:
    virtual void EnterHangar(ShipHangarModule* hangar) = 0;
    virtual void ExitHangar(ShipHangarModule* hangar) = 0;
};
// GravBike.h (inherits Vehicle)
class GravBike : public Vehicle {
public:
    GravBike(int Tier);
    void EnterHangar(ShipHangarModule* hangar) override;
    void ExitHangar(ShipHangarModule* hangar) override;

private:
    int Tier;
    ProceduralMesh BikeMesh;
    Vector3 DockedPosition;
};
// RoverVehicle.h (inherits Vehicle)
class RoverVehicle : public Vehicle {
public:
    RoverVehicle(int RoverClass);
    void EnterHangar(ShipHangarModule* hangar) override;
    void ExitHangar(ShipHangarModule* hangar) override;

private:
    int RoverClass;
    ProceduralMesh RoverMesh;
    Vector3 DockedPosition;
};

Perfect — let’s break ship turret generation and related ship module systems into a clear, implementable framework for EVEOFFLINE so it can be deterministic, procedural, and modular like the rest of the game systems.

Ship Turret & Module Generation Blueprint
1️⃣ Turret Classification
Type	Function	Placement Constraints	Procedural Notes
Forward-Facing Guns	Primary attack	Bow, nose, turret sockets	Always aligned to ship spine, small deviation for RNG spread
Gimbaled Turrets	Track targets 360°	On top decks or flanks	Procedural orientation based on ship class & size
Flak / Missile Defense	Anti-missile/torpedo	Above hull or behind main shields	Procedural arcs & cooldowns generated per class
Drone Launchers	Deploy combat/support drones	Near drone bay modules	Number of drones depends on bay tier & ship class
Heavy Weapons / Beam Arrays	Capital-level weaponry	Upper or central hull	Slot count scales with mass and module upgrades
Flares / ECM	Defensive countermeasures	Hull corners, flanks	Procedural effect visuals & cooldowns
2️⃣ Turret Placement Logic
Module-Driven Placement

Each hull module defines attachment sockets:

Weapon_Small
Weapon_Medium
Weapon_Large
Turret_Gimbal
Missile_Defense
Drone_Launcher
Generator checks module size & ship class before assigning turret type

Scaling by Ship Class

Frigate: 2–6 turrets, limited gimbals, minimal drone support

Destroyer: 8–16 turrets, mix of gimbaled & forward, small drone bay

Cruiser/Capital: 20+ turrets, multiple drone bays, flak & heavy weapons, secondary gun arrays

Functional Logic

Forward guns → high damage, low rotation

Gimbaled → moderate damage, tracks targets within arc radius

Anti-missile → triggers automatically on projectile detection

Drone launchers → spawn drones procedurally based on bay module tier

Exterior Influence

Turret modules deform the hull mesh slightly to accommodate size

Visible support structures, rails, and hull recesses generated procedurally

Can be upgraded with shields or reactive armor modules

3️⃣ Procedural Turret Generation (C++)
class ShipTurretGenerator {
public:
    ShipTurretGenerator(int Seed, ShipClass shipClass);

    void GenerateTurrets();
    void PlaceTurret(FVector SocketLocation, TurretType type, Module* parentModule);
    void ScaleTurretByShipClass(TurretType type, ShipClass shipClass);
    void AttachTurretVisuals(TurretType type, int UpgradeTier);

private:
    int Seed;
    ShipClass ShipClass;
    std::vector<Module*> ShipModules;
    std::vector<Turret*> Turrets;
};
Notes:

Seed-based RNG ensures deterministic procedural generation

Upgrade tiers affect size, visuals, and firepower

Turret placement respects hull shape and exterior mesh generation

4️⃣ Integration with Ship & Interior Systems
Turret generation reads module types: weapons, drone bays, missile arrays

Drone bays linked to internal storage modules, procedural elevators, and hangars

Visuals respond to ship faction style, procedural hull mesh, and upgrade tiers

Turrets can be modified in ship designer before deployment:

Swap turret type

Adjust rotation/gimbal angle

Upgrade ammo / fire control modules

5️⃣ Procedural Patterns & Variability
Hull Influence: Turrets cause slight procedural protrusions, support struts, or armor adjustments

Randomized Details:

Small vents, cables, or antenna near turrets

Color tint variations based on faction / procedural palette

RPG Stats Scaling:

Damage, range, reload time scaled by ship class + module tier

Special abilities (anti-missile flares, beam arcs, drone spawn rate)

Mod Validation Rules
