3️⃣ MULTIPLAYER HANDSHAKE + MOD VALIDATION FLOW
Connection Flow
Client -> Connect Request
Server -> Sends:
   - WorldSeed
   - PCGVersion
   - ModList + Versions
   - RequiredModsHash
Client Validation
bool ValidateMods(const ServerInfo& Server)
{
    if (LocalModHash != Server.RequiredModsHash)
        return false;

    if (LocalPCGVersion != Server.PCGVersion)
        return false;

    return true;
}
If Validation Fails
- Show diff list:
  ✔ Installed
  ✖ Missing
  ⚠ Version mismatch

Options:
- Auto-disable conflicting mods
- Download required mods
- Abort connection
Server Authority
Server is authoritative over:

PCG seeds

Ship generation

Loot generation

Salvage outcomes

Fleet movement

RTS orders

Clients are visual + input only.

#pragma once

MenuScreen.h (base class)
#pragma once

class MenuScreen
{
public:
    virtual ~MenuScreen() = default;

    virtual void OnEnter() {}
    virtual void OnExit() {}
    virtual void Update(float dt) {}
    virtual void Render() {}
};
MenuStateMachine.h
#pragma once
#include <memory>
#include <unordered_map>
#include "MenuState.h"
#include "MenuScreen.h"

class MenuStateMachine
{
public:
    void SetState(EMenuState newState);
    void Update(float dt);
    void Render();

    template<typename T>
    void RegisterScreen(EMenuState state);

private:
    EMenuState currentState = EMenuState::Boot;
    std::unordered_map<EMenuState, std::unique_ptr<MenuScreen>> screens;
};
MenuStateMachine.cpp
#include "MenuStateMachine.h"

void MenuStateMachine::SetState(EMenuState newState)
{
    if (screens[currentState])
        screens[currentState]->OnExit();

    currentState = newState;

    if (screens[currentState])
        screens[currentState]->OnEnter();
}

void MenuStateMachine::Update(float dt)
{
    if (screens[currentState])
        screens[currentState]->Update(dt);
}

void MenuStateMachine::Render()
{
    if (screens[currentState])
        screens[currentState]->Render();
}

template<typename T>
void MenuStateMachine::RegisterScreen(EMenuState state)
{
    screens[state] = std::make_unique<T>();
}
TitleScreen.cpp (example)
#include "TitleScreen.h"
#include "../MenuStateMachine.h"

void TitleScreen::Render()
{
    // Draw background starfield
    // Draw menu buttons

    if (UI::Button("New Game"))
        menu->SetState(EMenuState::CharacterCreation);

    if (UI::Button("Multiplayer"))
        menu->SetState(EMenuState::MultiplayerRoot);

    if (UI::Button("Mods"))
        menu->SetState(EMenuState::Mods);

    if (UI::Button("Exit"))
        menu->SetState(EMenuState::Shutdown);
}

5️⃣ TIE-IN TO ATLAS / EVEOFFLINE CORE
Application.cpp
void Application::Run()
{
    menu.RegisterScreen<TitleScreen>(EMenuState::Title);
    menu.RegisterScreen<ModsScreen>(EMenuState::Mods);
    menu.RegisterScreen<MultiplayerScreen>(EMenuState::MultiplayerRoot);

    menu.SetState(EMenuState::Title);

    while (running)
    {
        menu.Update(deltaTime);
        menu.Render();
    }
}

1️⃣ CHARACTER CREATION — FULL C++ PIPELINE
This is not just cosmetics. Character creation produces:

A deterministic CharacterSeed

A Stat Profile

A Faction + Race alignment

Hooks into skills, dialogue, rig access, and MP sync

CharacterCreationData.h
#pragma once
#include <string>
#include <cstdint>

enum class ERace
{
    Human,
    Synth,
    Voidborn,
    Exile
};

struct CharacterStats
{
    float Strength;
    float Agility;
    float Intelligence;
    float Perception;
};

struct CharacterCreationData
{
    uint64 CharacterSeed;

    ERace Race;
    std::string FactionID;

    CharacterStats BaseStats;

    // Cosmetic (safe to change later)
    uint32 BodyType;
    uint32 FacePreset;
};
CharacterCreationSystem.h
#pragma once
#include "CharacterCreationData.h"

class CharacterCreationSystem
{
public:
    CharacterCreationData CreateDefault();
    void Randomize(CharacterCreationData& data);
    void ApplyRaceModifiers(CharacterCreationData& data);

    uint64 GenerateSeed(const CharacterCreationData& data);
};
CharacterCreationSystem.cpp
#include "CharacterCreationSystem.h"
#include <functional>

CharacterCreationData CharacterCreationSystem::CreateDefault()
{
    CharacterCreationData data{};
    data.Race = ERace::Human;
    data.FactionID = "Neutral";
    data.BaseStats = { 5,5,5,5 };

    data.CharacterSeed = GenerateSeed(data);
    return data;
}

uint64 CharacterCreationSystem::GenerateSeed(const CharacterCreationData& data)
{
    std::hash<std::string> h;
    uint64 seed = static_cast<uint64>(data.Race);
    seed ^= h(data.FactionID);
    seed ^= (uint64)data.BodyType << 32;
    return seed;
}
MP Sync Rule
- CharacterSeed is sent to server
- Server validates race/faction
- Stats are recalculated server-side
🔥 Why this matters:
Everything downstream (animations, rigs, NPC reactions, starting gear, ship access) keys off this seed. No desync. No cheating.

5️⃣ PLANET → SPACE SEAMLESS TRANSITION
This is the crown jewel.

Key Rule
The world never changes coordinate systems.

World Zones
enum class EWorldZone
{
    PlanetSurface,
    Atmosphere,
    Orbital,
    DeepSpace
};
Transition Trigger
EWorldZone ResolveZone(float altitude)
{
    if (altitude < 2000.f) return EWorldZone::PlanetSurface;
    if (altitude < 10000.f) return EWorldZone::Atmosphere;
    if (altitude < 50000.f) return EWorldZone::Orbital;
    return EWorldZone::DeepSpace;
}
Streaming Behavior
PlanetSurface:
  - Terrain chunks
  - Buildings
  - NPCs

Atmosphere:
  - Clouds
  - Aerodynamics enabled

Orbital:
  - Gravity taper
  - Stations load

DeepSpace:
  - RTS overlay unlocks
  - Fleet controls
Camera Authority Shift
if (zone == EWorldZone::DeepSpace)
{
    Camera.SetMode(CameraMode::Strategic);
}
🔥 Why this matters:
No “enter space” cutscene. No instance swap.
The RTS layer becomes naturally justified.

    Structural,

class BuildGrid
{
public:

    bool CanPlace(int x, int y, int z) const;

    std::vector<GridCell> cells;

ModuleDefinition.h
#pragma once
#include <vector>
#include "SnapPoint.h"

struct ModuleDefinition
{
    std::string ModuleID;
    int SizeX, SizeY, SizeZ;

    int PowerDraw;
    int PowerGen;

    std::vector<ESnapType> AllowedSnapTypes;
};
Placement Logic
bool CanSnap(const ModuleDefinition& mod, const SnapPoint& snap)
{
    for (auto type : mod.AllowedSnapTypes)
        if (type == snap.Type)
            return true;
    return false;
}
🔥 Why this matters
Ruins can be half-usable

Ancient modules can violate modern rules

Ships/habitats share one placement system

Visuals are derived, not hardcoded

2️⃣ TURRET AI + FIRING ARCS
(Industrial → Military → Alien → Improvised)

Turrets are characters, not dumb guns.

TurretDefinition.h
#pragma once

enum class ETurretRole
{
    AntiFighter,
    AntiCapital,
    PointDefense,
    Mining,
    Salvage
};

struct TurretDefinition
{
    ETurretRole Role;

    float MinYaw, MaxYaw;
    float MinPitch, MaxPitch;

    float RotationSpeed;
    float OptimalRange;
};
TurretTargeting.h
#pragma once

struct TargetData
{
    float Distance;
    float Velocity;
    bool IsMissile;
};
TurretAI.cpp
bool IsTargetInArc(const TurretDefinition& turret, float yaw, float pitch)
{
    return yaw >= turret.MinYaw &&
           yaw <= turret.MaxYaw &&
           pitch >= turret.MinPitch &&
           pitch <= turret.MaxPitch;
}

float TargetPriority(const TargetData& target, ETurretRole role)
{
    if (role == ETurretRole::PointDefense && target.IsMissile)
        return 100.f;

    return 1.f / target.Distance;
}
Firing Logic
if (IsTargetInArc(turret, yaw, pitch))
{
    LeadTarget();
    FireIfSolutionValid();
}
🔥 Why this matters
Salvage turrets behave differently than combat turrets

Alien turrets can bend arc rules

Improvised turrets jitter, overheat, misalign

Thresholds
+75 Allied
+25 Friendly
  0 Neutral

Consequence Hooks
if (rep < -75)
{
    SpawnBountyHunters();

    UnlockMilitaryBlueprints();

CrewMember.h
#pragma once
#include <string>

enum class ECrewRole
{
    Pilot,
    Engineer,
    Gunner,
    Medic,
    Scientist
};

struct CrewMember
{
    std::string Name;
    ECrewRole Role;

    float Skill;
    float Fatigue;
    float Morale;
};
CrewSystem.h
#pragma once
#include <vector>
#include "CrewMember.h"

class CrewSystem
{
public:
    void Update(float dt);
    float GetEfficiency(ECrewRole role) const;

private:
    std::vector<CrewMember> crew;
};
Example Effect
float CrewSystem::GetEfficiency(ECrewRole role) const
{
    float total = 0.f;
    for (auto& c : crew)
        if (c.Role == role)
            total += c.Skill * (1.f - c.Fatigue);

    return total;
}
Systems Affected
Pilots → maneuverability
Engineers → repair speed
Gunners → turret tracking
Scientists → scan depth
Medics → recovery speed
🔥 Why this matters
Boarding kills crew = long-term damage

Automation ≠ replacement

Ships feel unique over time

5️⃣ BOARDING & BREACH GAMEPLAY
(FPS + systemic destruction)

No teleporting. No canned scenes.

BreachPoint.h
#pragma once

struct BreachPoint
{
    float HullIntegrity;
    bool IsExposed;
};
Breach Logic
void ApplyBreach(BreachPoint& bp, float damage)
{
    bp.HullIntegrity -= damage;
    if (bp.HullIntegrity <= 0)
        bp.IsExposed = true;
}
Breach Consequences
- Atmosphere loss
- Fire
- Crew panic
- AI system failures
Boarding Flow
EVA →
Cut hull →
Zero-G interior →
FPS combat →
Loot / sabotage →
Escape or capture ship
Ship Capture Rule
bool CanCaptureShip()
{
    return CrewAlive < 20% && BridgeControlled;
}
🔥 Why this matters
Capital ships become dungeons

War feeds salvage loops

You can steal ships without destroying them

🔗 HOW ALL FIVE SYSTEMS FEED EACH OTHER
Build Mode → Ship Layout
Ship Layout → Turret Arcs
Turrets → Crew Efficiency
Crew Loss → Reputation
Reputation → War
War → Debris Fields
Debris → Salvage
Salvage → New Modules
That’s a closed economic + combat loop.
